# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka Log Compaction Architecture

## Your Task

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the domain domain.

- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)

- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

64-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the analysis of Kafka's log compaction architecture and created the answer file. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I identified all the Java source files in apache/kafka that implement log compaction:

### **Core Components:**

1. **Cleaner Thread** (`LogCleaner.java`):
   - The `LogCleaner` class manages a pool of `CleanerThread` instances that continuously perform background log cleaning
   - Each thread executes the main cleaning loop via `doWork()`, alternating between cleaning logs and pausing

2. **Segment Selection Policy** (`LogCleanerManager.java`):
   - The `grabFilthiestCompactedLog()` method implements the policy by selecting logs based on "cleanable ratio" (dirty bytes / total bytes)
   - Filters for compact retention policy logs and selects the dirtiest one first
   - Uses `cleanableOffsets()` to determine which parts of a log need cleaning

3. **Key-Based Deduplication Logic**:
   - **`Cleaner.java`**: Core deduplication engine with:
     - `buildOffsetMap()`: Creates key=>last_offset mapping for dirty sections
     - `shouldRetainRecord()`: Determines if a record should be retained based on its key's latest offset
     - `cleanInto()`: Filters records during copying
     - `groupSegmentsBySize()`: Selects segments to clean together
   
   - **`SkimpyOffsetMap.java`**: Hash table implementation using cryptographic hashing (MD5)
     - `put()`: Stores key hashes and offsets
     - `get()`: Retrieves offsets for deduplication lookups

The answer includes 12 core files and identifies the key methods and symbols involved in the log compaction process.

java.util.concurrent.TimeUnit;\\n45: import java.util.function.Function;\\n46: import java.util.stream.Collectors;\\n47: import java.util.stream.IntStream;\\n48: \\n49: /**\\n50:  * The cleaner is responsible for removing obsolete records from logs which have the \\\"compact\\\" retention strategy.\\n51:  * A message with key K and offset O is obsolete if there exists a message with key K and offset O' such that O < O'.\\n52:  * <p>\\n53:  * Each log can be thought of being split into two sections of segments: a \\\"clean\\\" section which has previously been cleaned followed by a\\n54:  * \\\"dirty\\\" section that has not yet been cleaned. The dirty section is further divided into the \\\"cleanable\\\" section followed by an \\\"uncleanable\\\" section.\\n55:  * The uncleanable section is excluded from cleaning. The active log segment is always uncleanable. If there is a\\n56:  * compaction lag time set, segments whose largest message timestamp is within the compaction lag time of the cleaning operation are also uncleanable.\\n57:  * <p>\\n58:  * The cleaning is carried out by a pool of background threads. Each thread chooses the dirtiest log that has the \\\"compact\\\" retention policy\\n59:  * and cleans that. The dirtiness of the log is guessed by taking the ratio of bytes in the dirty section of the log to the total bytes in the log.\\n60:  * <p>\\n61:  * To clean a log the cleaner first builds a mapping of key=>last_offset for the dirty section of the log. See {@link OffsetMap} for details of\\n62:  * the implementation of the mapping.\\n63:  * <p>\\n64:  * Once the key=>last_offset map is built, the log is cleaned by recopying each log segment but omitting any key that appears in the offset map with a\\n65:  * higher offset than what is found in the segment (i.e. messages with a key that appears in the dirty section of the log).\\n66:  * <p>\\n67:  * To avoid segments shrinking to very small sizes with repeated cleanings we implement a rule by which if we will merge successive segments when\\n68:  * doing a cleaning if their log and index size are less than the maximum log and index size prior to the clean beginning.\\n69:  * <p>\\n70:  * Cleaned segments are swapped into the log as they become available.\\n71:  * <p>\\n72:  * One nuance that the cleaner must handle is log truncation. If a log is truncated while it is being cleaned the cleaning of that log is aborted.\\n73:  * <p>\\n74:  * Messages with null payload are treated as deletes for the purpose of log compaction. This means that they receive special treatment by the cleaner.\\n75:  * The cleaner will only retain delete records for a period of time to avoid accumulating space indefinitely. This period of time is configurable on a per-topic\\n76:  * basis and is measured from the time the segment enters the clean portion of the log (at which point any prior message with that key has been removed).\\n77:  * Delete markers in the clean section of the log that are older than this time will not be retained when log segments are being recopied as part of cleaning.\\n78:  * This time is tracked by setting the base timestamp of a record batch with delete markers when the batch is recopied in the first cleaning that encounters\\n79:  * it. The relative timestamps of the records in the batch are also modified when recopied in this cleaning according to the new base timestamp of the batch.\\n80:  * <p>\\n81:  * Note that cleaning is more complicated with the idempotent/transactional producer capabilities. The following\\n82:  * are the key points:\\n83:  * <p>\\n84:  * <ol>\\n85:  * <li>In order to maintain sequence number continuity for active producers, we always retain the last batch\\n86:  *    from each producerId, even if all the records from the batch have been removed. The batch will be removed\\n87:  *    once the producer either writes a new batch or is expired due to inactivity.</li>\\n88:  * <li>We do not clean beyond the last stable offset. This ensures that all records observed by the cleaner have\\n89:  *    been decided (i.e. committed or aborted). In particular, this allows us to use the transaction index to\\n90:  *    collect the aborted transactions ahead of time.</li>\\n91:  * <li>Records from aborted transactions are removed by the cleaner immediately without regard to record keys.</li>\\n92:  * <li>Transaction markers are retained until all record batches from the same transaction have been removed and\\n93:  *    a sufficient amount of time has passed to reasonably ensure that an active consumer wouldn't consume any\\n94:  *    data from the transaction prior to reaching the offset of the marker. This follows the same logic used for\\n95:  *    tombstone deletion.</li>\\n96:  * </ol>\\n97:  */\\n98: public class LogCleaner implements BrokerReconfigurable {\\n99:     private static final Logger java.util.stream.Collectors;\n47: import java.util.stream.IntStream;\n48: \n49: /**\n50:  * The cleaner is responsible for removing obsolete records from logs which have the \"compact\" retention strategy.\n51:  * A message with key K and offset O is obsolete if there exists a message with key K and offset O' such that O < O'.\n52:  * <p>\n53:  * Each log can be thought of being split into two sections of segments: a \"clean\" section which has previously been cleaned followed by a\n54:  * \"dirty\" section that has not yet been cleaned. The dirty section is further divided into the \"cleanable\" section followed by an \"uncleanable\" section.\n55:  * The uncleanable section is excluded from cleaning. The active log segment is always uncleanable. If there is a\n56:  * compaction lag time set, segments whose largest message timestamp is within the compaction lag time of the cleaning operation are also uncleanable.\n57:  * <p>\n58:  * The cleaning is carried out by a pool of background threads. Each thread chooses the dirtiest log that has the \"compact\" retention policy\n59:  * and cleans that. The dirtiness of the log is guessed by taking the ratio of bytes in the dirty section of the log to the total bytes in the log.\n60:  * <p>\n61:  * To clean a log the cleaner first builds a mapping of key=>last_offset for the dirty section of the log. See {@link OffsetMap} for details of\n62:  * the implementation of the mapping.\n63:  * <p>\n64:  * Once the key=>last_offset map is built, the log is cleaned by recopying each log segment but omitting any key that appears in the offset map with a\n65:  * higher offset than what is found in the segment (i.e. messages with a key that appears in the dirty section of the log).\n66:  * <p>\n67:  * To avoid segments shrinking to very small sizes with repeated cleanings we implement a rule by which if we will merge successive segments when\n68:  * doing a cleaning if their log and index size are less than the maximum log and index size prior to the clean beginning.\n69:  * <p>\n70:  * Cleaned segments are swapped into the log as they become available.\n71:  * <p>\n72:  * One nuance that the cleaner must handle is log truncation. If a log is truncated while it is being cleaned the cleaning of that log is aborted.\n73:  * <p>\n74:  * Messages with null payload are treated as deletes for the purpose of log compaction. This means that they receive special treatment by the cleaner.\n75:  * The cleaner will only retain delete records for a period of time to avoid accumulating space indefinitely. This period of time is configurable on a per-topic\n76:  * basis and is measured from the time the segment enters the clean portion of the log (at which point any prior message with that key has been removed).\n77:  * Delete markers in the clean section of the log that are older than this time will not be retained when log segments are being recopied as part of cleaning.\n78:  * This time is tracked by setting the base timestamp of a record batch with delete markers when the batch is recopied in the first cleaning that encounters\n79:  * it. The relative timestamps of the records in the batch are also modified when recopied in this cleaning according to the new base timestamp of the batch.\n80:  * <p>\n81:  * Note that cleaning is more complicated with the idempotent/transactional producer capabilities. The following\n82:  * are the key points:\n83:  * <p>\n84:  * <ol>\n85:  * <li>In order to maintain sequence number continuity for active producers, we always retain the last batch\n86:  *    from each producerId, even if all the records from the batch have been removed. The batch will be removed\n87:  *    once the producer either writes a new batch or is expired due to inactivity.</li>\n88:  * <li>We do not clean beyond the last stable offset. This ensures that all records observed by the cleaner have\n89:  *    been decided (i.e. committed or aborted). In particular, this allows us to use the transaction index to\n90:  *    collect the aborted transactions ahead of time.</li>\n91:  * <li>Records from aborted transactions are removed by the cleaner immediately without regard to record keys.</li>\n92:  * <li>Transaction markers are retained until all record batches from the same transaction have been removed and\n93:  *    a sufficient amount of time has passed to reasonably ensure that an active consumer wouldn't consume any\n94:  *    data from the transaction prior to reaching the offset of the marker. This follows the same logic used for\n95:  *    tombstone deletion.</li>\n96:  * </ol>\n97:  */\n98: public class LogCleaner implements BrokerReconfigurable {\n99:     private static final Logger LOG = LoggerFactory.getLogger(LogCleaner.class);\n100: \n101:     public static final Set<String> RECONFIGURABLE_CONFIGS = Set.of(\n102:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_THREADS_PROP,\n103:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_DEDUPE_BUFFER_SIZE_PROP,\n104:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_DEDUPE_BUFFER_LOAD_FACTOR_PROP,\n105:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_IO_BUFFER_SIZE_PROP,\n106:             ServerConfigs.MESSAGE_MAX_BYTES_CONFIG,\n107:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_IO_MAX_BYTES_PER_SECOND_PROP,\n108:             CleanerConfig.LOG_CLEANER_BACKOFF_MS_PROP\n109:     );\n110: \n111:     // Visible for test\n112:     public static final String MAX_BUFFER_UTILIZATION_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME = \"max-buffer-utilization-percent\";\n113:     public static final String MAX_CLEAN_TIME_METRIC_NAME = \"max-clean-time-secs\";\n114:     public static final String MAX_COMPACTION_DELAY_METRICS_NAME = \"max-compaction-delay-secs\";\n115: \n116:     private static final String CLEANER_RECOPY_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME = \"cleaner-recopy-percent\";\n117:     private static final String DEAD_THREAD_COUNT_METRIC_NAME = \"DeadThreadCount\";\n118: \n119:     // Visible for test\n120:     public static final Set<String> METRIC_NAMES = Set.of(\n121:             MAX_BUFFER_UTILIZATION_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME,\n122:             CLEANER_RECOPY_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME,\n123:             MAX_CLEAN_TIME_METRIC_NAME,\n124:             MAX_COMPACTION_DELAY_METRICS_NAME,\n125:             DEAD_THREAD_COUNT_METRIC_NAME\n126:     );\n127: \n128:     // For compatibility, metrics are registerMetrics() {\n174:         /* a metric to track the maximum utilization of any thread's buffer in the last cleaning */\n175:         metricsGroup.newGauge(MAX_BUFFER_UTILIZATION_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME,\n176:                 () -> (int) (maxOverCleanerThreads(t -> t.lastStats.bufferUtilization) * 100));\n177: \n178:         /* a metric to track the recopy rate of each thread's last cleaning */\n179:         metricsGroup.newGauge(CLEANER_RECOPY_PERCENT_METRIC_NAME, () -> {\n180:             List<CleanerStats> stats = cleaners.stream().map(t -> t.lastStats).toList();\n181:             double recopyRate = (double) stats.stream().mapToLong(stat -> stat.bytesWritten).sum() /\n182:                     Math.max(stats.stream().mapToLong(stat -> stat.bytesRead).sum(), 1);\n183:             return (int) (100 * recopyRate);\n184:         });\n185: \n186:         /* a metric to track the maximum cleaning time for the last cleaning from each thread */\n187:         metricsGroup.newGauge(MAX_CLEAN_TIME_METRIC_NAME, () -> (int) maxOverCleanerThreads(t -> t.lastStats.elapsedSecs()));\n188: \n189:         // a metric to track delay between the time when a log is required to be compacted\n190:         // as determined by max compaction lag and the time of last cleaner run.\n191:         metricsGroup.newGauge(MAX_COMPACTION_DELAY_METRICS_NAME,\n192:                 () -> (int) (maxOverCleanerThreads(t -> (double) t.lastPreCleanStats.maxCompactionDelayMs()) / 1000));\n193: \n194:         metricsGroup.newGauge(DEAD_THREAD_COUNT_METRIC_NAME, this::deadThreadCount);\n195:     }\n196: \n197:     /**\n198:      * Start the background cleaner threads.\n199:      */\n200:     public void startup() {\n201:         if (config.numThreads < 1) {\n202:             LOG.warn(\"Invalid value for `log.cleaner.threads`: must be >= 1 starting from Kafka 5.0 since log cleaner\" +\n203:                     \" is always enabled.\");\n204:         }\n205: \n206:         LOG.info(\"Starting the log cleaner\");\n207:         IntStream.range(0, config.numThreads).forEach(i -> {\n208:             try (NoSuchAlgorithmException e) {\n213:                 throw new RuntimeException(e);\n214:             }\n215:         });\n216:     }\n217: \n218:     /**\n219:      * Stop the background cleaner                thread.shutdown();\n226:             } catch (InterruptedException e) {\n227:                 throw new RuntimeException(e);\n228:             }\n229:         });\n230:         cleaners.clear();\n231:     }\n232: \n233:     /**\n234:      * Stop the background cleaner threads.\n235:      */\n236:     public void shutdown() {\n237:         try {\n238: /**\n261:      * Validate the new cleaner threads num is reasonable.\n262:      *\n263:      * @param newConfig A submitted new AbstractConfig instance that contains new cleaner config\n264:      */\n265:     @Override\n266:     public void validateReconfiguration(AbstractConfig newConfig) {\n267:         int numThreads = new CleanerConfig(newConfig).numThreads;\n268:         int currentThreads = config.numThreads;\n269:         if (numThreads < 1)\n270:             throw new ConfigException(\"Log cleaner threads should be at least 1\");\n271:         if (numThreads < currentThreads / 2)\n272:             throw new ConfigException(\"Log cleaner threads cannot be reduced to less than half the current value \" + currentThreads);\n273:         if (numThreads > currentThreads * 2)\n274:             throw new ConfigException(\"Log cleaner threads cannot be increased to more than double the current value \" + currentThreads);\n275: \n276:     }\n277: \n278:     /**\n279:      * Reconfigure log clean config. This method waits until the\n376:      * cleaner has processed up to the given offset on the specified topic/partition.\n377:      *\n378:      * @param topicPartition The topic and partition to be cleaned\n379:      * @param offset The first dirty offset that the cleaner doesn't have to clean\n380:      * @param maxWaitMs The maximum time in ms to wait for cleaner\n381:      *\n382:      *     }\n393: \n394:     private boolean isCleaned(TopicPartition topicPartition, long offset) {\n395:         return \n400:     /**\n401:      * To prevent race between retention and compaction,\n402:      * retention threads need to make this call to obtain:\n403:      *\n404:      * @return A map of log partitions that retention threads can safely work on\n405:      */\n406:     public Map<TopicPartition, UnifiedLog> pauseCleaningForNonCompactedPartitions() {\n407:         return Each thread processes does its cleaning repeatedly by\n465:      * choosing the dirtiest log, cleaning it, and then swapping in the cleaned segments.\n466:      */\n467:     public class CleanerThread extends ShutdownableThread {\n468:         private final Logger logger = new LogContext(logPrefix).logger(CleanerThread.class);\n469: \n470:         private final Cleaner cleaner;\n471: \n472:         private volatile CleanerStats lastStats = new CleanerStats(Time.SYSTEM);\n473:         private volatile PreCleanStats lastPreCleanStats = new PreCleanStats();\n474: \n475:         @SuppressWarnings(\"this-escape\")\n476:         public CleanerThread(int threadId) throws NoSuchAlgorithmException {\n477:             super(\"kafka-log-cleaner-thread-\" + threadId, false);\n478: \n479:             cleaner = new Cleaner(\n480:                     threadId,\n481:                     new SkimpyOffsetMap((int) Math.min(config.dedupeBufferSize / config.numThreads, Integer.MAX_VALUE), config.hashAlgorithm()),\n482:                     config.ioBufferSize / config.numThreads / 2,\n483:                     config.maxMessageSize,\n484:                     config.dedupeBufferLoadFactor,\n485:                     throttler,\n486:                     time,\n487:                     this::checkDone\n488:             );\n489: \n490:             if (config.dedupeBufferSize / config.numThreads > Integer.MAX_VALUE) {\n491:                 logger.warn(\"Cannot use more than 2G of cleaner buffer space per cleaner thread, ignoring excess buffer space...\");\n492:             }\n493:         }\n494: \n495:         /**\n496:          *  Check if the cleaning for a partition is aborted. Marking its partition ({}) as uncleanable\", e.log, e.log.topicPartition(), e);\n548:                 cleanerManager.markPartitionUncleanable(e.log.parentDir(), e.log.topicPartition());\n549: \n550:                 return false;\n551:             }\n552:         }\n553: \n554:         private boolean cleanFilthiestLog() throws LogCleaningException {\n555:             PreCleanStats preCleanStats = new PreCleanStats();\n556:             Optional<LogToClean> ltc = cleanerManager.grabFilthiestCompactedLog(time, preCleanStats);\n557:             boolean cleaned;\n558: \n559:             if (ltc.isEmpty()) {\n560:                 cleaned = false;\n561:             } else {\n562:                 // there's a log, clean it\n563:                 this.lastPreCleanStats = preCleanStats;\n564:                 LogToClean cleanable = ltc.get();\n565:                 try {\n566:                     cleanLog(cleanable);\n567:                     cleaned = true;\n568:                 } catch (ThreadShutdownException e) {\n569:                     throw e;\n570:                 } catch (Exception e) {\n571:                     throw new LogCleaningException(cleanable.log(), e.getMessage(), e);\n572:                 }\n573:             }\n574: \n575:             Map<TopicPartition, UnifiedLog> deletable = cleanerManager.deletableLogs();\n576:             try {\n577: \"storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/Cleaner.java\", \"symbol\": \"shouldRetainRecord\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"Kafka's log compaction architecture consists of three main components: the cleaner thread, segment selection policy, and key-based deduplication logic.\\n\\n**Cleaner Thread**: The LogCleaner class (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleaner.java) manages a pool of CleanerThread instances that continuously perform background log cleaning. Each CleanerThread inherits from ShutdownableThread and executes the main cleaning loop via the doWork() method, which alternates between cleaning the filthiest log and pausing when no cleanable logs exist.\\n\\n**Segment Selection Policy**: The LogCleanerManager class (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleanerManager.java) implements the segment selection policy through the grabFilthiestCompactedLog() method. This method selects logs for cleaning based on the \\\"cleanable ratio\\\" - the ratio of dirty bytes to total bytes. The method filters for logs with compact retention policy that are not already in progress, calculates cleanable offsets via cleanableOffsets(), and returns the log with the highest cleanable ratio. This ensures the dirtiest logs are cleaned first, optimizing I/O usage.\\n\\n**Key-Based Deduplication Logic**: The actual deduplication happens in the Cleaner class (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/Cleaner.java). The key methods are:\\n\\n1. buildOffsetMap() (line 635-681) - Constructs a key=>last_offset mapping for the dirty section of the log using the OffsetMap interface.\\n\\n2. SkimpyOffsetMap implementation (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/SkimpyOffsetMap.java) - A hash table using cryptographic hashing (MD5 by default) to deduplicate keys with collision resolution via probing. The put() method (line 134-164) stores key hashes and offsets, updating existing entries or adding new ones. The get() method (line 107-126) retrieves the offset for a given key hash.\\n\\n3. shouldRetainRecord() method (line 492-527) - The core deduplication logic that determines if a record should be retained during cleaning. It checks if the record has the latest offset for its key using the offset map. Records are retained if they have a value or cannot be deleted yet (based on delete retention policies).\\n\\n4. cleanInto() method (line 306-415) - Uses a MemoryRecords.RecordFilter to iterate through source records and apply the shouldRetainRecord() logic, filtering out obsolete records and writing retained records to the cleaned segment.\\n\\n5. groupSegmentsBySize() method (line 566-601) - Selects which segments to group together during cleaning, ensuring groups don't exceed maximum log/index sizes to prevent excessive segment shrinkage.\\n\\nThe cleaning flow: CleanerThread.doWork() \u2192 grabFilthiestCompactedLog() \u2192 Cleaner.clean() \u2192 buildOffsetMap() \u2192 cleanSegments() \u2192 cleanInto() \u2192 shouldRetainRecord() using SkimpyOffsetMap for fast lookups of the latest offset for each key.\\n\\nSupporting classes include CleanerConfig (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/CleanerConfig.java) for configuration, CleanerStats and PreCleanStats for metrics, LogCleaningState (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogCleaningState.java) for state management, LogToClean (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogToClean.java) representing a log to clean, and CleanedTransactionMetadata (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/CleanedTransactionMetadata.java) for managing transaction state during cleaning.\"\n}\n",
